## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces (Duffing-type), nonlinear damping (van der Pol-type), or external time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Coulomb-like damping with restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**2 * v + c3 * v (combined Duffing + van der Pol)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * v (position-dependent stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry x → -x
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping (self-excitation or limit cycles as in van der Pol)
- Cubic velocity terms v**3 → Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation distinguishing small vs large amplitude behavior
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Product x * cos(c*t) → parametric excitation where the natural frequency is modulated in time
- Absence of explicit t dependence → autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated without external input
- Linear v term with negative coefficient → energy injection (negative damping) leading to self-sustained oscillations
- Ratio of cubic to linear coefficient in x determines hardening (same sign) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior

GT Equivalence Verification (PO30)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - beta*sin(v) - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0884*v³ - 0.1959*v*sin(x) - 3.998*x³ - 0.1959*sin(v)`

The GT has four terms:
1. `c₀*x³` (coefficient ≈ -3.998)
2. `c₁*v³` (coefficient ≈ -0.0884)
3. `c₂*v*sin(x)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1959)
4. `c₃*sin(v)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1959)

The key challenge is matching `sin(x)*v` and `sin(v)`. These are transcendental functions that cannot be represented by polynomial terms alone.

Let me check which candidates contain non-polynomial terms that could potentially represent `sin(x)` or `sin(v)`:

**Candidates with exp():** 3, 5, 11, 13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 21, 33, 39, 40 — exp() cannot equal sin().

**Candidates with log():** 4, 6, 7, 18, 19 — log() cannot equal sin().

**Candidates with Abs():** 22, 25, 26, 27, 28, 29, 30, 31, 32, 40, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46, 47, 48 — |v| is NOT equivalent to v (since v can be negative), and these can't produce sin().

**Candidates with cos(t):** 25, 33, 40, 41, 50 — cos(c*t) depends on t, not on x or v, so can't match sin(x) or sin(v).

**Candidates with sin():** 49 has `sin(c₂ + c₃*v*x)` and `cos(c₇*v²*x)` — these have arguments involving products of v and x, not sin(x) alone or sin(v) alone.

**Pure polynomial candidates:** 1, 2, 8, 9, 10, 12, 20, 23, 24, 34, 35, 36, 37, 38 — These only have polynomial terms in x and v. They cannot represent sin(x)*v or sin(v).

Now let me think about whether any candidate could approximate the GT through Taylor expansion. The GT contains `sin(x)` and `sin(v)`, which have Taylor expansions:
- `sin(x) = x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - ...`
- `sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`

So `v*sin(x) = v*x - v*x³/6 + v*x⁵/120 - ...`
And `sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`

The GT becomes approximately:
- `-3.998*x³ - 0.0884*v³ - 0.1959*(v*x - v*x³/6 + v*x⁵/120 - ...) - 0.1959*(v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...)`

This gives terms: `x³, v³, v*x, v*x³, v*x⁵, v, v⁵, ...` etc.

But mathematical equivalence requires **exact** equality, not approximation. A polynomial can never exactly equal a function containing sin(). The Taylor series of sin() has infinitely many terms, and no finite polynomial can reproduce it.

Therefore, **no candidate** can be made exactly equivalent to the GT, because:
- All candidates are either polynomials, or contain exp/log/Abs/cos(t) terms, none of which can produce `sin(x)*v` or `sin(v)`.
- Candidate 49 has sin and cos but with wrong argument structures (`sin(c + c*v*x)` and `cos(c*v²*x)`) that cannot be reduced to `sin(x)` or `sin(v)`.

[NO MATCH]

- `x³`
- `v³`
- `v*sin(x)`
- `sin(v)`

Key insight: `sin(v)` and `v*sin(x)` are transcendental functions. They cannot be exactly represented by polynomials or other elementary functions. Let me check each candidate.

**Taylor expansion reference:**
- `sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - v⁷/5040 + ...`
- `sin(x) = x - x³/6 + x⁵/120 - x⁷/5040 + ...`
- So `v*sin(x) = v*x - v*x³/6 + v*x⁵/120 - v*x⁷/5040 + ...`
- And `sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - v⁷/5040 + ...`

The GT has `sin(v)` and `v*sin(x)` which are infinite series. No finite polynomial can exactly match these. Similarly, `exp()`, `log()`, and `Abs()` cannot exactly reproduce `sin()`.

Let me check candidates that might have the right structure:

**Candidates 1-48, 50:** These are all combinations of polynomial terms, `exp()`, `log()`, `Abs()`, and `cos(t)` terms. None contain `sin(x)` or `sin(v)`. Since `sin` cannot be exactly represented by any finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, or absolute values, none of these can match.

**Candidate 49:** `c0*v + c1*sin(c2 + c3*v*x) + c4*v³ + c5*x³ + c6*cos(c7*v²*x) + c8*v³*x + c9*v*x⁵`

We need `sin(x)` (function of x only) and `sin(v)` (function of v only) separately. There's no way to decompose `sin(c2 + c3*v*x)` into `v*sin(x) + sin(v)`. This cannot match.

Let me verify all candidates systematically - none contain both `sin(x)` and `sin(v)` as separate terms, or any structure that could produce them. Therefore, no candidate matches.
